href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/220px-Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/330px-Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/440px-Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1840" data-file-height="1150" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Building_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Building of the European Parliament in Brussels</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg/220px-%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg" width="220" height="641" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg/330px-%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg/440px-%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg 2x" data-file-width="991" data-file-height="2887" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%22European_Parliament%22_on_official_languages_of_the_European_Union.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"European Parliament" in official languages of the European Union (on the Parliament building in Brussels)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>European Parliament</b> (<b>EP</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">directly elected</a> parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institution of the European Union (EU)</a>. Together with the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> (the Council) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, it exercises the legislative function of the EU. The Parliament is composed of 751 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">members</a>, who represent the second-largest democratic electorate in the world (after the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_India" title="Parliament of India">Parliament of India</a>) and the largest trans-national democratic electorate in the world (375&#160;million eligible <a href="/wiki/Voting" title="Voting">voters</a> in 2009).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18_new_MEPs_take_their_seats_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18_new_MEPs_take_their_seats-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It has been directly elected every five years by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> since 1979. However, <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a> at <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in the European Union">European Parliament elections</a> has fallen consecutively at each election since that date, and has been under 50% since 1999. Voter turnout in 2014 stood at 42.54% of all European voters.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the European Parliament has legislative power that the Council and Commission do not possess, it does not formally possess <a href="/wiki/Legislative_initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative initiative">legislative initiative</a>, as most <a href="/wiki/National_parliaments_of_the_European_Union" title="National parliaments of the European Union">national parliaments</a> of European Union member states do.<sup id="cite_ref-Parliament&#39;s_powers_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament&#39;s_powers-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pot_initiative_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pot_initiative-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The Parliament is the "first institution" of the EU (mentioned first in the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>, having ceremonial precedence over all authority at European level),<sup id="cite_ref-Protocol_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Protocol-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and shares equal legislative and budgetary powers with the Council (except in a few areas where the <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union#Special_legislative_procedures" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislature of the European Union">special legislative procedures</a> apply). It likewise has equal control over the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EU budget</a>. Finally, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the executive body of the EU, is accountable to Parliament. In particular, Parliament elects the President of the Commission, and approves (or rejects) the appointment of the Commission as a whole. It can subsequently force the Commission as a body to resign by adopting a motion of censure.<sup id="cite_ref-Parliament&#39;s_powers_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament&#39;s_powers-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a> (Parliament\'s <a href="/wiki/Speaker_(politics)" title="Speaker (politics)">speaker</a>) is <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tajani" title="Antonio Tajani">Antonio Tajani</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">EPP</a>), elected in January 2017. He presides over a multi-party chamber, the two largest groups being the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party_(European_Parliament_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="European People&#39;s Party (European Parliament group)">Group of the European People\'s Party</a> (EPP) and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats</a> (S&amp;D). The last union-wide elections were the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014" title="European Parliament election, 2014">2014 elections</a>.\n</p><p>The European Parliament has three places of work&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> (Belgium), <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">the city of Luxembourg</a> (Luxembourg) and <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> (France).\nLuxembourg is home to the administrative offices (the "General Secretariat"). Meetings of the whole Parliament ("plenary sessions") take place in Strasbourg and in Brussels. Committee meetings are held in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaty_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaty-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#References"><span links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a></div>\n<p>The Parliament, like the other institutions, was not designed in its current form when it first met on 10 September 1952. One of the oldest common institutions, it began as the <i>Common Assembly</i> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC). It was a consultative assembly of 78 appointed parliamentarians <a href="/wiki/Dual_mandate" title="Dual mandate">drawn</a> from the national parliaments of member states, having no legislative powers.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The change since its foundation was highlighted by Professor David Farrell of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester" title="University of Manchester">University of Manchester</a>: "For much of its life, the European Parliament could have been justly labelled a \'multi-lingual talking shop\'."<sup id="cite_ref-Farrell_Powerful_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farrell_Powerful-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Its development since its foundation shows how the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>\'s structures have evolved without a clear "master plan". Some, such as Tom Reid of the <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i>, said of the union: "nobody would have deliberately designed a government as complex and as redundant as the EU".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Even the Parliament\'s <a href="/wiki/Location_of_European_Union_institutions#European_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Location of European Union institutions">two seats</a>, which have switched several times, are a result of various agreements or lack of agreements. Although most <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a> would prefer to be based just in Brussels, at <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a>\'s 1992 Edinburgh <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">summit</a>, France engineered a treaty amendment to maintain Parliament\'s plenary seat permanently at Strasbourg.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consultative_assembly">Consultative assembly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Consultative assembly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>\nThe body was not mentioned in the original <a href="/wiki/Schuman_Declaration" title="Schuman Declaration">Schuman Declaration</a>. It was assumed or hoped that difficulties with the British would be resolved to allow the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">Council of Europe\'s Assembly</a> to perform the task. A separate Assembly was introduced during negotiations on the Treaty as an institution which would counterbalance and monitor the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> while providing democratic legitimacy.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The wording of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">ECSC Treaty</a> demonstrated the leaders\' desire for more than a normal consultative assembly by using the term "representatives of the people" and allowed for direct election. Its early importance was highlighted when the Assembly was given the task of drawing up the draft treaty to establish a <a href="/wiki/European_Political_Community" title="European Political Community">European Political Community</a>. By this document, the Ad Hoc Assembly was established on 13 September 1952<sup id="cite_ref-AEIpolitical_union_draft_treaty_1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AEIpolitical_union_draft_treaty_1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> with extra members, but after the failure of the proposed <a href="/wiki/European_Defence_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Defence Community">European Defence Community</a> the project was dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_composition_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_composition-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002,_Stra%C3%9Fburg,_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002%2C_Stra%C3%9Fburg%2C_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002%2C_Stra%C3%9Fburg%2C_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002%2C_Stra%C3%9Fburg%2C_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002%2C_Stra%C3%9Fburg%2C_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002%2C_Stra%C3%9Fburg%2C_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002%2C_Stra%C3%9Fburg%2C_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="583" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F023908-0002,_Stra%C3%9Fburg,_Tagung_des_Europarates.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Session of the Council of Europe\'s Assembly in the former <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Europe" title="Palace of Europe">House of Europe</a> in Strasbourg in January 1967. <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Foreign_Affairs_(Germany)" title="Minister for Foreign Affairs (Germany)">West German minister for Foreign Affairs</a>, is speaking.</div></div></div>\n<p>Despite this, the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euratom" class="mw-redirect" title="Euratom">Euratom</a> were established in 1958 by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaties of Rome</a>. The Common Assembly was shared by all three communities (which had separate executives) and it renamed itself the <i>European Parliamentary Assembly</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The first meeting was held on 19 March 1958 having been set up in Luxembourg, it elected Schuman as its president and on 13 May it rearranged itself to sit according to political ideology rather than nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-1958_history_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1958_history-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This is seen as the birth of the modern European Parliament, with Parliament\'s 50 years celebrations being held in March 2008 rather than 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-50_years_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50_years-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The three communities <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">merged</a> their remaining organs as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> in 1967, and the body\'s name was changed to the current "European Parliament" in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 1970 the Parliament was granted power over areas of the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">Communities\' budget</a>, which were expanded to the whole budget in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_Budget_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Budget-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Under the Rome Treaties, the Parliament should have become elected. However, the Council was required to agree a uniform voting system beforehand, which it failed to do. The Parliament threatened to take the Council to the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a>; this led to a compromise whereby the Council would agree to elections, but the issue of voting systems would be put off until a later date.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoskyns_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoskyns-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elected_Parliament">Elected Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Elected Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_European_Parliament_1973-1983.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The emblem of Parliament until 1983</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg/220px-Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg/330px-Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg/440px-Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4158" data-file-height="2974" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europa_Parlament_1985.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Session April 1985</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1979, its members were <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in the European Union">directly elected</a> for the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_1979" title="European Parliament election, 1979">first time</a>. This sets it apart from similar institutions such as those of the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">Pan-African Parliament</a> which are appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> After that first election, the parliament held its first session on 11 July 1979, electing <a href="/wiki/Simone_Veil" title="Simone Veil">Simone Veil</a> MEP as its president. Veil was also the first female president of the Parliament since it was formed as the Common Assembly.\n</p><p>As an elected body, the Parliament began to draft proposals addressing the functioning of the EU. For example, in 1984, inspired by its previous work on the Political Community, it drafted the "draft Treaty establishing the European Union" (also known as the \'Spinelli Plan\' after its rapporteur <a href="/wiki/Altiero_Spinelli" title="Altiero Spinelli">Altiero Spinelli</a> MEP). Although it was not adopted, many ideas were later implemented by other treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_TEU_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_TEU-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the Parliament began holding votes on proposed <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">Commission Presidents</a> from the 1980s, before it was given any formal right to veto.<sup id="cite_ref-Commission_Appointment_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission_Appointment-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nSince it became an elected body, the membership of the European Parliament has simply expanded whenever new nations have joined (the membership was also adjusted upwards in 1994 after <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>). Following this, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nice" title="Treaty of Nice">Treaty of Nice</a> imposed a cap on the number of members to be elected, 732.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_History_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_History-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pleniere.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Pleniere.JPG/220px-Pleniere.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Pleniere.JPG/330px-Pleniere.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Pleniere.JPG/440px-Pleniere.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3443" data-file-height="2282" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pleniere.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Europe" title="Palace of Europe">Palace of Europe</a>, Parliament\'s Strasbourg hemicycle until 1999</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg/220px-EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg/330px-EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg/440px-EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3918" data-file-height="2289" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EuropeanParliamentBuildingStrasbourgFrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>European Parliament Building in Strasbourg, France, view from street.</div></div></div>\n<p>Like the other institutions, the Parliament\'s <a href="/wiki/Seat_(legal_entity)" title="Seat (legal entity)">seat</a> was not yet fixed. The provisional arrangements placed Parliament in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, while the Commission and Council had their seats in Brussels. In 1985 the Parliament, wishing to be closer to these institutions, built a second chamber in Brussels and moved some of its work there despite protests from some states. A final agreement was eventually reached by the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> in 1992. It stated the Parliament would retain its formal seat in Strasbourg, where twelve sessions a year would be held, but with all other parliamentary activity in Brussels. This two-seat arrangement was contested by the Parliament, but was later enshrined in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amsterdam" title="Treaty of Amsterdam">Treaty of Amsterdam</a>. To this day the <a href="/wiki/Location_of_European_Union_institutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Location of European Union institutions">institution\'s locations</a> are a source of contention.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_seats_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_seats-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Parliament gained more powers from successive treaties, namely through the extension of the <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">ordinary legislative procedure</a> (then called the codecision procedure),<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_legis_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_legis-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and in 1999, the Parliament forced the resignation of the <a href="/wiki/Santer_Commission" title="Santer Commission">Santer Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The Parliament had refused to approve the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">Community budget</a> over allegations of fraud and mis-management in the Commission. The two main parties took on a government-opposition dynamic for the first time during the crisis which ended in the Commission resigning en masse, the first of any forced resignation, in the face of an impending censure from the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringe_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringe-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament_pressure_on_the_Commission">Parliament pressure on the Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Parliament pressure on the Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg/220px-Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg/330px-Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg/440px-Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso_MEDEF_FULL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2004, Parliament forced <a href="/wiki/President_Barroso" class="mw-redirect" title="President Barroso">President Barroso</a> to change his proposed Commission team.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2004, following the largest trans-national election in history, despite the European Council choosing a President from the largest political group (the EPP), the Parliament again exerted pressure on the Commission. During the Parliament\'s hearings of the proposed <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">Commissioners</a> MEPs raised doubts about some nominees with the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Civil_Liberties,_Justice_and_Home_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee on Civil Liberties, Justice and Home Affairs">Civil Liberties committee</a> rejecting <a href="/wiki/Rocco_Buttiglione" title="Rocco Buttiglione">Rocco Buttiglione</a> from the post of <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Justice,_Freedom_and_Security" class="mw-redirect" title="European Commissioner for Justice, Freedom and Security">Commissioner for Justice, Freedom and Security</a> over his views on homosexuality. That was the first time the Parliament had ever voted against an incoming Commissioner and despite Barroso\'s insistence upon Buttiglione the Parliament forced Buttiglione to be withdrawn. A number of other Commissioners also had to be withdrawn or reassigned before Parliament allowed the <a href="/wiki/Barroso_Commission" title="Barroso Commission">Barroso Commission</a> to take office.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_Butt_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_Butt-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rocco_Buttiglione_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Rocco_Buttiglione_2001.jpg/170px-Rocco_Buttiglione_2001.jpg" width="170" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/Rocco_Buttiglione_2001.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="205" data-file-height="279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rocco_Buttiglione_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rocco_Buttiglione" title="Rocco Buttiglione">Rocco Buttiglione</a> was the first Commission designate to be voted down by Parliament</div></div></div>\n<p>Along with the extension of the ordinary legislative procedure, the Parliament\'s democratic mandate has given it greater control over legislation against the other institutions. In voting on the <a href="/wiki/Bolkestein_directive" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolkestein directive">Bolkestein directive</a> in 2006, the Parliament voted by a large majority for over 400 amendments that changed the fundamental principle of the law. The <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> described it in the following terms:<sup id="cite_ref-FT_CIO_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT_CIO-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>That is where the European parliament has suddenly come into its own. It marks another shift in power between the three central EU institutions. Last week\'s vote suggests that the directly elected MEPs, in spite of their multitude of ideological, national and historical allegiances, have started to coalesce as a serious and effective EU institution, just as enlargement has greatly complicated negotiations inside both the Council and Commission.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>In 2007, for the first time, Justice Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Franco_Frattini" title="Franco Frattini">Franco Frattini</a> included Parliament in talks on the second <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Information_System" title="Schengen Information System">Schengen Information System</a> even though MEPs only needed to be consulted on parts of the package. After that experiment, Frattini indicated he would like to include Parliament in all justice and criminal matters, informally pre-empting the new powers they could gain as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frattini_2009_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frattini_2009-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Between 2007 and 2009, a <a href="/wiki/Special_working_group_on_parliamentary_reform" title="Special working group on parliamentary reform">special working group on parliamentary reform</a> implemented a series of changes to modernise the institution such as more speaking time for rapporteurs, increase committee co-operation and other efficiency reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-REFO12_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REFO12-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-REFO3_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REFO3-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Barroso_Commission" title="Barroso Commission">Barroso Commission</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolkestein.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bolkestein.png/170px-Bolkestein.png" width="170" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bolkestein.png/255px-Bolkestein.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bolkestein.png/340px-Bolkestein.png 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="1048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolkestein.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parliament\'s overhaul of the <a href="/wiki/Bolkestein_directive" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolkestein directive">Bolkestein directive</a> signalled a major growth in status for Parliament</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> finally came into force on 1 December 2009, granting Parliament powers over the entire <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EU budget</a>, making Parliament\'s <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">legislative powers</a> equal to the Council\'s in nearly all areas and linking the appointment of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">Commission President</a> to Parliament\'s own elections.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_info_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution_info-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Despite some calls for the parties to put forward candidates beforehand, only the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">EPP</a> (which had re-secured their position as largest party) had one in re-endorsing Barroso.<sup id="cite_ref-Epin_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Epin-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barroso gained the support of the European Council for a second term and secured majority support from the Parliament in September 2009. Parliament voted 382 votes in favour and 219 votes against (117 abstentions ) with support of the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Conservatives_and_Reformists" title="European Conservatives and Reformists">European Conservatives and Reformists</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe">Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-B2V_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B2V-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The liberals gave support after Barroso gave them a number of concessions; the liberals previously joined the socialists\' call for a delayed vote (the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">EPP</a> had wanted to approve Barroso in July of that year).<sup id="cite_ref-B2C_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B2C-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Once Barroso put forward the candidates for his next Commission, another opportunity to gain concessions arose. Bulgarian nominee <a href="/wiki/Rumiana_Jeleva" title="Rumiana Jeleva">Rumiana Jeleva</a> was forced to step down by Parliament due to concerns over her experience and financial interests. She only had the support of the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">EPP</a> which began to retaliate on left wing candidates before Jeleva gave in and was replaced (setting back the final vote further).<sup id="cite_ref-RJ_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RJ-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before the final vote, Parliament demanded a number of concessions as part of a future working agreement under the new Lisbon Treaty. The deal includes that Parliament\'s President will attend high level Commission meetings. Parliament will have a seat in the EU\'s Commission-lead international negotiations and have a right to information on agreements. However, Parliament secured only an observer seat. Parliament also did not secure a say over the appointment of <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_European_Union" title="List of diplomatic missions of the European Union">delegation</a> heads and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Special_Representative" title="European Union Special Representative">special representatives</a> for foreign policy. Although they will appear before parliament after they have been appointed by the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative" class="mw-redirect" title="High Representative">High Representative</a>. One major internal power was that Parliament wanted a pledge from the Commission that it would put forward legislation when parliament requests. Barroso considered this an infringement on the Commission\'s powers but did agree to respond within three months. Most requests are already responded to positively.<sup id="cite_ref-B2A_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B2A-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the setting up of the <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a> (EEAS), Parliament used its control over the EU budget to influence the shape of the EEAS. MEPs had aimed at getting greater oversight over the EEAS by linking it to the Commission and having political deputies to the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative</a>. MEPs didn\'t manage to get everything they demanded. However, they got broader financial control over the new body.<sup id="cite_ref-EEAS_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEAS-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_and_functions">Powers and functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Powers and functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/300px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" width="300" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/450px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/600px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="3389" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Parliament\'s hemicycle (<a href="/wiki/Debating_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Debating chamber">debating chamber</a>) during a plenary session in Strasbourg.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Parliament and Council have been compared to the two <a href="/wiki/Chambers_of_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Chambers of parliament">chambers</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> However, there are some differences from <a href="/wiki/National_parliaments_of_the_European_Union" title="National parliaments of the European Union">national legislatures</a>; for example, neither the Parliament nor the Council have the power of <a href="/wiki/Legislative_initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative initiative">legislative initiative</a> (except for the fact that the Council has the power in some <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism#A_theory_of_regional_integration" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmental</a> matters). In <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">Community matters</a>, this is a power uniquely reserved for the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> (the executive). Therefore, while Parliament can amend and reject legislation, to make a proposal for legislation, it needs the Commission to draft a <a href="/wiki/Bill_(proposed_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill (proposed law)">bill</a> before anything can become law.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The value of such a power has been questioned by noting that in the national legislatures of the member states 85% of initiatives introduced without executive support fail to become law.<sup id="cite_ref-Kreppel_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kreppel-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Yet it has been argued by former Parliament president <a href="/wiki/Hans-Gert_P%C3%B6ttering" title="Hans-Gert P\xc3\xb6ttering">Hans-Gert P\xc3\xb6ttering</a> that as the Parliament does have the right to ask the Commission to draft such legislation, and as the Commission is following Parliament\'s proposals more and more Parliament does have a <i>de facto</i> right of legislative initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-Pot_initiative_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pot_initiative-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Parliament also has a great deal of indirect influence, through <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law#Legislation" title="European Union law">non-binding resolutions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Committees_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Committees of the European Parliament">committee hearings</a>, as a "pan-European <a href="/wiki/Soapbox" title="Soapbox">soapbox</a>" with the ear of <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union#Lobbyists_and_journalists" title="Brussels and the European Union">thousands of Brussels-based journalists</a>. There is also an indirect effect on <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">foreign policy</a>; the Parliament must approve all development grants, including those overseas. For example, the support for <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">post-war Iraq</a> reconstruction, or incentives for the cessation of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran" title="Nuclear program of Iran">Iranian nuclear development</a>, must be supported by the Parliament. Parliamentary support was also required for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">transatlantic</a> passenger data-sharing deal with the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Rockwell_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rockwell-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Finally, Parliament holds a non-binding vote on new EU treaties but cannot veto it. However, when Parliament threatened to vote down the Nice Treaty, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Federal_Parliament" title="Belgian Federal Parliament">Belgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of Italy">Italian Parliaments</a> said they would veto the treaty on the European Parliament\'s behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_procedure">Legislative procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Legislative procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With each new treaty, the powers of the Parliament, in terms of its role in the <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">Union\'s legislative procedures</a>, have expanded. The procedure which has slowly become dominant is the "<a href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">ordinary legislative procedure</a>" (previously named "codecision procedure"), which provides an equal footing between Parliament and Council. In particular, under the procedure, the Commission presents a proposal to Parliament and the Council which can only become law if both agree on a text, which they do (or not) through successive readings up to a maximum of three. In its first reading, Parliament may send amendments to the Council which can either adopt the text with those amendments or send back a "common position". That position may either be approved by Parliament,  or it may reject the text by an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute majority">absolute majority</a>, causing it to fail, or it may adopt further amendments, also by an absolute majority. If the Council does not approve these, then a "Conciliation Committee" is formed. The Committee is composed of the Council members plus an equal number of MEPs who seek to agree a compromise. Once a position is agreed, it has to be approved by Parliament, by a simple majority.<sup id="cite_ref-Parliament&#39;s_powers_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament&#39;s_powers-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-decision_making_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decision_making-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> This is also aided by Parliament\'s mandate as the only directly democratic institution, which has given it leeway to have greater control over legislation than other institutions, for example over its changes to the <a href="/wiki/Bolkestein_directive" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolkestein directive">Bolkestein directive</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-FT_CIO_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT_CIO-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The few other areas that operate the <i>special legislative procedures</i> are justice &amp; home affairs, budget and taxation and certain aspects of other policy areas: such as the fiscal aspects of environmental policy. In these areas, the Council or Parliament decide law alone.<sup id="cite_ref-lisbon_explain_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lisbon_explain-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The procedure also depends upon which type of <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law#Legislation" title="European Union law">institutional act</a> is being used.<sup id="cite_ref-Parliament&#39;s_powers_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parliament&#39;s_powers-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The strongest act is a <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union)" title="Regulation (European Union)">regulation</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">act</a> or <a href="/wiki/Statutory_law" title="Statutory law">law</a> which is directly applicable in its entirety. Then there are <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union)" title="Directive (European Union)">directives</a> which bind member states to certain goals which they must achieve. They do this through their own laws and hence have room to manoeuvre in deciding upon them. A <a href="/wiki/European_Union_decision" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union decision">decision</a> is an instrument which is focused at a particular person or group and is directly applicable. Institutions may also issue <a href="/wiki/European_Union_recommendation" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union recommendation">recommendations and opinions</a> which are merely non-binding, declarations.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> There is a further document which does not follow normal procedures, this is a "written declaration" which is similar to an <a href="/wiki/Early_day_motion" title="Early day motion">early day motion</a> used in the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>. It is a document proposed by up to five MEPs on a matter within the EU\'s activities used to launch a debate on that subject. Having been posted outside the entrance to the hemicycle, members can sign the declaration and if a majority do so it is forwarded to the President and announced to the plenary before being forwarded to the other institutions and formally noted in the minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-EP_WD_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EP_WD-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The legislative branch officially holds the Union\'s budgetary authority with powers gained through the <a href="/wiki/Budgetary_treaties_of_the_European_Communities" title="Budgetary treaties of the European Communities">Budgetary Treaties</a> of the 1970s and the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EU budget</a> is subject to a form of the ordinary legislative procedure with a single reading giving Parliament power over the entire budget (before 2009, its influence was limited to certain areas) on an equal footing to the Council. If there is a disagreement between them, it is taken to a conciliation committee as it is for legislative proposals. If the joint conciliation text is not approved, the Parliament may adopt the budget definitively.<sup id="cite_ref-lisbon_explain_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lisbon_explain-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Parliament is also responsible for discharging the implementation of previous budgets based on the annual report of the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a>. It has refused to approve the budget only twice, in 1984 and in 1998. On the latter occasion it led to the resignation of the <a href="/wiki/Santer_Commission" title="Santer Commission">Santer Commission</a>; highlighting how the budgetary power gives Parliament a great deal of power over the Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoskyns_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoskyns-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ringe_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringe-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-budget_background_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-budget_background-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Parliament also makes extensive use of its budgetary, and other powers, elsewhere; for example in the setting up of the <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a>, Parliament has a de facto veto over its design as it has to approve the budgetary and staff changes.<sup id="cite_ref-EEAS_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEAS-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_of_the_executive">Control of the executive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Control of the executive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> is proposed by the European Council on the basis of the European elections to Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_info_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution_info-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> That proposal has to be approved by the Parliament (by a simple majority) who "elect" the President according to the treaties. Following the approval of the Commission President, the members of the Commission are proposed by the President in accord with the member states. Each Commissioner comes before a relevant parliamentary committee hearing covering the proposed portfolio. They are then, as a body, approved or rejected by the Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Commission_Oversight_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission_Oversight-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In practice, the Parliament has never voted against a President or his Commission, but it did seem likely when the Barroso Commission was put forward. The resulting pressure forced the proposal to be withdrawn and changed to be more acceptable to parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_Butt_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_Butt-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> That pressure was seen as an important sign by some of the evolving nature of the Parliament and its ability to make the Commission accountable, rather than being a rubber stamp for candidates. Furthermore, in voting on the Commission, MEPs also voted along party lines, rather than national lines, despite frequent pressure from national governments on their MEPs. This cohesion and willingness to use the Parliament\'s power ensured greater attention from national leaders, other institutions and the public\xe2\x80\x94who previously gave the lowest ever turnout for the Parliament\'s elections.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Parliament also has the power to censure the Commission if they have a two-thirds majority which will force the resignation of the entire Commission from office. As with approval, this power has never been used but it was threatened to the <a href="/wiki/Santer_Commission" title="Santer Commission">Santer Commission</a>, who subsequently <a href="/wiki/Santer_Commission#Resignation" title="Santer Commission">resigned of their own accord</a>. There are a few other controls, such as: the requirement of Commission to submit reports to the Parliament and answer questions from MEPs; the requirement of the President-in-office of the Council to present its programme at the start of their <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">presidency</a>; the obligation on the President of the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> to report to Parliament after each of its meetings; the right of MEPs to make requests for legislation and policy to the Commission; and the right to question members of those institutions (e.g. "Commission <a href="/wiki/Question_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Question Time">Question Time</a>" every Tuesday).<sup id="cite_ref-Commission_Appointment_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission_Appointment-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Commission_Oversight_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commission_Oversight-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> At present, MEPs may ask a question on any topic whatsoever, but in July 2008 MEPs voted to limit questions to those within the EU\'s mandate and ban offensive or personal questions.<sup id="cite_ref-EUO_rise_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_rise-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supervisory_powers">Supervisory powers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Supervisory powers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Parliament also has other powers of general supervision, mainly granted by the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The Parliament has the power to set up a Committee of Inquiry, for example over mad cow disease or CIA detention flights\xe2\x80\x94the former led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Medicines_Agency" title="European Medicines Agency">European veterinary agency</a>. The Parliament can call other institutions to answer questions and if necessary to take them to <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Communities" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Justice of the European Communities">court</a> if they break EU law or treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-supervisory_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supervisory-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, it has powers over the appointment of the members of the Court of Auditors<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and the president and executive board of the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_European_Central_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the European Central Bank">ECB president</a> is also obliged to present an annual report to the parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-supervisory_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supervisory-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Ombudsman" title="European Ombudsman">European Ombudsman</a> is elected by the Parliament, who deals with public complaints against all institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-supervisory_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supervisory-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Citizens%27_Initiative" title="European Citizens&#39; Initiative">Petitions</a> can also be brought forward by any <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">EU citizen</a> on a matter within the EU\'s sphere of activities. The <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Petitions" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee on Petitions">Committee on Petitions</a> hears cases, some 1500 each year, sometimes presented by the citizen themselves at the Parliament. While the Parliament attempts to resolve the issue as a mediator they do resort to legal proceedings if it is necessary to resolve the citizens dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-petitions_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petitions-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin: 0 1em 0.5em; clear:right">\n<caption><b>National apportionment of MEP seats (total 751)</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>\n<table style="font-size: 95%; width: 290px;" cellpadding="1" cellspacing="0">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a></td>\n<td><div style="width: 96px; height: 4px; background: #555555;"></div></td>\n<td style="border-top: 1px solid #aaaaaa;">6 (0.8%)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Member of the European Parliament</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">parliamentarians</a> are known in English as Members of the European Parliament (MEPs). They are elected every five years by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal adult suffrage</a> and sit according to political allegiance; about a third are women. Before 1979 they were appointed by their national parliaments.<sup id="cite_ref-ENA_composition_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_composition-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EP_Members_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EP_Members-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under the Lisbon Treaty, <a href="/wiki/Apportionment_in_the_European_Parliament" title="Apportionment in the European Parliament">seats are allocated</a> to each state according to population and the maximum number of members is set at 751 (however, as the President cannot vote while in the chair there will only be 750 voting members at any one time).<sup id="cite_ref-EUO_Lisbon_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_Lisbon-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The seats are distributed according to "<a href="/wiki/Degressive_proportionality" title="Degressive proportionality">degressive proportionality</a>", i.e., the larger the state, the more citizens are represented per MEP. As a result, Maltese and Luxembourgish voters have roughly 10x more influence per voter than citizens of the six large countries.\n</p><p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Germany (80.9 million inhabitants) has 96 seats (previously 99 seats), i.e. one seat for 843,000 inhabitants. Malta (0.4 million inhabitants) has 6 seats, i.e. one seat for 70,000 inhabitants.\n</p><p>The new system implemented under the Lisbon Treaty, including revising the seating well before elections, was intended to avoid political <a href="/wiki/Horse_trading_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse trading (political)">horse trading</a> when the allocations have to be revised to reflect demographic changes.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pursuant to this apportionment, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_constituency" title="European Parliament constituency">constituencies</a> are formed. In six EU member states (Belgium, France, Ireland, Italy, Poland, and the United Kingdom), the national territory is divided into a number of constituencies. In the remaining member states, the whole country forms a single constituency. All member states hold elections to the European Parliament using various forms of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transitional_arrangements">Transitional arrangements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transitional arrangements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Due to the delay in ratifying the Lisbon Treaty, the <a href="/wiki/7th_European_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="7th European Parliament">seventh parliament</a> was elected under the lower Nice Treaty cap. A <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union#Transitional_provisions_protocol" title="Treaties of the European Union">small scale treaty amendment</a> was ratified on 29 November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This amendment brought in transitional provisions to allow the 18 additional MEPs created under the Lisbon Treaty to be elected or appointed before the 2014 election.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Under the Lisbon Treaty reforms, Germany was the only state to lose members from 99 to 96. However, these seats were not removed until the 2014 election.<sup id="cite_ref-extra_meps_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extra_meps-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Salaries_and_expenses">Salaries and expenses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Salaries and expenses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before 2009, members received the same salary as members of their national parliament. However, from 2009 a new members statute came into force, after years of attempts, which gave all members an equal monthly pay, of \xe2\x82\xac8,020.53 each in 2014, subject to a European Union tax and which can also be taxed nationally. MEPs are entitled to a pension, paid by Parliament, from the age of 63. Members are also entitled to allowances for office costs and subsistence, and travelling expenses, based on actual cost.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (January 2016)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Besides their pay, members are granted a number of privileges and <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_immunity" title="Diplomatic immunity">immunities</a>. To ensure their free movement to and from the Parliament, they are accorded by their own states the facilities accorded to senior officials travelling abroad and, by other state governments, the status of visiting <a href="/wiki/Diplomat" title="Diplomat">foreign representatives</a>. When in their own state, they have all the immunities accorded to national parliamentarians, and, in other states, they have immunity from <a href="/wiki/Detention_(imprisonment)" title="Detention (imprisonment)">detention</a> and <a href="/wiki/Criminal_procedure" title="Criminal procedure">legal proceedings</a>. However, immunity cannot be claimed when a member is found committing a criminal offence and the Parliament also has the right to strip a member of their immunity.<sup id="cite_ref-LEX_Prot_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LEX_Prot-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_groups">Political groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Political groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">Political groups of the European Parliament</a></div>\n<p>MEPs in Parliament are organised into seven different <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_group" title="Parliamentary group">parliamentary groups</a>, including thirty non-attached members known as <i><a href="/wiki/Non-inscrits" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-inscrits">non-inscrits</a></i>. The two largest groups are the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a> (EPP) and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Socialists &amp; Democrats</a> (S&amp;D). These two groups have dominated the Parliament for much of its life, continuously holding between 50 and 70 percent of the seats between them. No single group has ever held a majority in Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> As a result of being broad alliances of national parties, European group parties are very decentralised and hence have more in common with parties in federal states like Germany or the United States than unitary states like the majority of the EU states.<sup id="cite_ref-Kreppel_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kreppel-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, the European groups were actually more cohesive than their US counterparts between 2004 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Groups are often based on a single <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">socialist group</a> (before 2009). However, they can, like the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe">liberal group</a>, include more than one European party as well as national parties and independents.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> For a group to be recognised, it needs 25 MEPs from seven different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Once recognised, groups receive financial subsidies from the parliament and guaranteed seats on committees, creating an incentive for the formation of groups. However, some controversy occurred with the establishment of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Identity,_Tradition,_Sovereignty" title="Identity, Tradition, Sovereignty">Identity, Tradition, Sovereignty</a> (ITS) due to its ideology; the members of the group were far-right, so there were concerns about public funds going towards such a group.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_ITS_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_ITS-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> There were attempts to change the rules to block the formation of ITS, but they never came to fruition. The group was, however, blocked from gaining leading positions on committees&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 traditionally (by agreement, not a rule) shared among all parties.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> When this group engaged in infighting, leading to the withdrawal of some members, its size fell below the threshold for recognition causing its collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_coalition">Grand coalition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Grand coalition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Given that the Parliament does not form the government in the traditional sense of a Parliamentary system, its politics have developed along more consensual lines rather than <a href="/wiki/Majority_rule" title="Majority rule">majority rule</a> of competing parties and coalitions. Indeed, for much of its life it has been dominated by a <a href="/wiki/Grand_coalition" title="Grand coalition">grand coalition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a>. The two major parties tend to co-operate to find a compromise between their two groups leading to proposals endorsed by huge majorities.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> However, this does not always produce agreement, and each may instead try to build other alliances, the EPP normally with other centre-right or right wing Groups and the PES with centre-left or left wing Groups. Sometimes, the Liberal Group is then in the pivotal position. There are also occasions where very sharp party political divisions have emerged, for example over the <a href="/wiki/Santer_Commission#Budget_controversy" title="Santer Commission">resignation of the Santer Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringe_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringe-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When the initial allegations against the Commission emerged, they were directed primarily against <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dith_Cresson" title="\xc3\x89dith Cresson">\xc3\x89dith Cresson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Manuel Mar\xc3\xadn">Manuel Mar\xc3\xadn</a>, both socialist members. When the parliament was considering refusing to discharge the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">Community budget</a>, President <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Santer" title="Jacques Santer">Jacques Santer</a> stated that a no vote would be tantamount to a <a href="/wiki/Vote_of_no_confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Vote of no confidence">vote of no confidence</a>. The Socialist group supported the Commission and saw the issue as an attempt by the EPP to discredit their party ahead of the 1999 elections. Socialist leader, <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Green" title="Pauline Green">Pauline Green</a> MEP, attempted a vote of confidence and the EPP put forward counter motions. During this period the two parties took on similar roles to a government-<a href="/wiki/Opposition_(parliamentary)" title="Opposition (parliamentary)">opposition</a> dynamic, with the Socialists supporting the executive and EPP renouncing its previous coalition support and voting it down.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringe_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringe-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Politicisation such as this has been increasing, in 2007 Simon Hix of the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics</a> noted that:<sup id="cite_ref-Farrell_Powerful_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farrell_Powerful-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Our work also shows that politics in the European Parliament is becoming increasingly based around party and ideology. Voting is increasingly split along left-right lines, and the cohesion of the party groups has risen dramatically, particularly in the fourth and fifth parliaments. So there are likely to be policy implications here too.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>During the fifth term, 1999 to 2004, there was a break in the grand coalition resulting in a centre-right coalition between the Liberal and People\'s parties.<sup id="cite_ref-Watson_interview_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson_interview-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> This was reflected in the Presidency of the Parliament with the terms being shared between the EPP and the ELDR, rather than the EPP and Socialists.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In the following term the liberal group grew to hold 88 seats, the largest number of seats held by any third party in Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-ALDE_formed_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALDE_formed-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Elections_to_the_European_Parliament" title="Elections to the European Parliament">Elections to the European Parliament</a></div>\n<table align="right" border="0" style="background:none">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><div class="thumbinner" style="width:570px">\n<table style="background: transparent; border: 0; padding: 0; margin: 0; width:570px" cellspacing="0">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:570px; background:white; height:200px; padding: 0; margin: 0;" class="thumbimage"><div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_86b6bea58f11c021b70a110257250046"></map><img usemap="#timeline_86b6bea58f11c021b70a110257250046" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/86b6bea58f11c021b70a110257250046.png" /></div>\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<td style="padding: 0; margin: 0; border: 0;" colspan="3"><div class="thumbcaption">The composition of the European Parliament with regard to percental share of deputies for each political group, 1979 to 2014. Left to right;<br />\n<table style="background:none; width:100%">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block;
