width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C10000; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_United_Left%E2%80%93Nordic_Green_Left" title="European United Left\xe2\x80\x93Nordic Green Left">Radical left</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F10000; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_of_Socialists_and_Democrats" title="Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats">Socialists</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #009900; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_Greens%E2%80%93European_Free_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="European Greens\xe2\x80\x93European Free Alliance">Greens and regionalists</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_Green_Party" title="European Green Party">Greens</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #999999; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Technical_Group_of_Independents_(1979%E2%80%931984)" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical Group of Independents (1979\xe2\x80\x931984)">CDI</a> or <a href="/wiki/Technical_Group_of_Independents_(1999%E2%80%932001)" title="Technical Group of Independents (1999\xe2\x80\x932001)">TGI</a></div>\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #999999; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Non-Inscrits" title="Non-Inscrits">Non-Inscrits</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF00; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe">Liberals</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF00; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_Radical_Alliance" title="European Radical Alliance">Radical Alliance</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3399FF; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">CD/EPP</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3399FF; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Forza_Europa" title="Forza Europa">Forza Europa</a></div>\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000EB; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_Conservatives_and_Reformists" title="European Conservatives and Reformists">Conservatives</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF9900; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Europe_of_Freedom_and_Direct_Democracy" title="Europe of Freedom and Direct Democracy">Eurosceptics</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #99FFFF; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Union_for_Europe_of_the_Nations" title="Union for Europe of the Nations">UEN</a></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000000; color:black; font-size:7pt; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/European_Right_(1989%E2%80%931994)" class="mw-redirect" title="European Right (1989\xe2\x80\x931994)">Far-right</a></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Elections have taken place, directly in every member state, every five years since 1979. As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there have been eight elections. When a nation joins mid-term, a by-election will be held to elect their representatives. This has happened six times, most recently when Croatia joined in 2013. Elections take place across four days according to local custom and, apart from having to be proportional, the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_system" title="Electoral system">electoral system</a> is chosen by the member state.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> This includes allocation of <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_constituency" title="European Parliament constituency">sub-national constituencies</a>; while most members have a national list, some, like the UK and France, divide their allocation between regions. Seats are allocated to member states according to their population, since 2014 with no state having more than 96, but no fewer than 6, to maintain proportionality.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The most recent Union-wide elections to the European Parliament were the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014" title="European Parliament election, 2014">European elections of 2014</a>, held from 22 to 25 May 2014. They were the largest simultaneous transnational elections ever held anywhere in the world.\nThe eighth term of Parliament started on 1 July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The proportion of MEPs elected in 2009 who were female was 35%; in 1979 it was just 16.5%.\n</p><p>There have been a number of proposals designed to attract greater public attention to the elections. One such innovation in the 2014 elections was that the <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">pan-European political parties</a> fielded "candidates" for <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">president</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">Commission</a>, the so-called <i>Spitzenkandidaten</i> (German, "leading candidates" or "top candidates"). However, European Union governance is based on a mixture of intergovernmental and supranational features: the President of the European Commission is nominated by the European Council, representing the governments of the member states, and there is no obligation for them to nominate the successful "candidate". The Lisbon Treaty merely states that they should take account of the results of the elections when choosing whom to nominate. The so-called <i>Spitzenkandidaten</i> were  <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a> for the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guy_Verhofstadt" title="Guy Verhofstadt">Guy Verhofstadt</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Liberals_and_Democrats_for_Europe_Party" title="Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe Party">Alliance of Liberals and Democrats for Europe Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ska_Keller" title="Ska Keller">Ska Keller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Bov%C3%A9" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Bov\xc3\xa9">Jos\xc3\xa9 Bov\xc3\xa9</a> jointly for the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Party" title="European Green Party">European Green Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Tsipras" title="Alexis Tsipras">Alexis Tsipras</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_the_European_Left" title="Party of the European Left">Party of the European Left</a>.\n</p><p>Turnout has dropped consistently every year since the first election, and from 1999 it has been below 50%. In 2007 both <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2007" title="European Parliament election, 2007">Bulgaria and Romania elected their MEPs</a> in by-elections, having joined at the beginning of 2007. The Bulgarian and Romanian elections saw two of the lowest turnouts for European elections, just 28.6%<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and 28.3% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In England, Scotland and Wales, EP elections were originally held for a constituency MEP on a first-past-the-post basis.  In 1999 the system was changed to a form of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">PR</a> where a large group of candidates would stand for a post within a very large regional constituency.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  One could vote for a party, but not a candidate (unless that party had a single candidate).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proceedings">Proceedings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Proceedings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels,_Belgium_2016_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels%2C_Belgium_2016_02.jpg/250px-European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels%2C_Belgium_2016_02.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels%2C_Belgium_2016_02.jpg/375px-European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels%2C_Belgium_2016_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels%2C_Belgium_2016_02.jpg/500px-European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels%2C_Belgium_2016_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parlament_Hemicycle_Bryssels,_Belgium_2016_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The hemicycle in Brussels.</div></div></div>\n<p>Each year the activities of the Parliament cycle between committee weeks where reports are discussed in committees and interparliamentary delegations meet, political group weeks for members to discuss work within their political groups and session weeks where members spend 3\xc2\xbd days in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> for part-sessions. In addition six 2-day part-sessions are organised in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> throughout the year. Four weeks are allocated as constituency week to allow members to do exclusively constituency work. Finally there are no meetings planned during the summer weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The Parliament has the power to meet without being convened by another authority. Its meetings are partly controlled by the treaties but are otherwise up to Parliament according to its own "Rules of Procedure" (the regulations governing the parliament).<sup id="cite_ref-rules_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rules-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During sessions, members may speak after being called on by the President. Members of the Council or Commission may also attend and speak in debates.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Partly due to the need for translation, and the politics of consensus in the chamber, debates tend to be calmer and more polite than, say, the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Voting is conducted primarily by a show of hands, that may be checked on request by electronic voting.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Votes of MEPs are not recorded in either case, however; that only occurs when there is a roll-call ballot. This is required for the final votes on legislation and also whenever a political group or 30 MEPs request it. The number of roll-call votes has increased with time. Votes can also be a completely secret ballot (for example, when the president is elected).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> All recorded votes, along with minutes and legislation, are recorded in the <i><a href="/wiki/Official_Journal_of_the_European_Union" title="Official Journal of the European Union">Official Journal of the European Union</a></i> and can be accessed online.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Votes usually do not follow a debate, but rather they are grouped with other due votes on specific occasions, usually at noon on Tuesdays, Wednesdays or Thursdays. This is because the length of the vote is unpredictable and if it continues for longer than allocated it can disrupt other debates and meetings later in the day.<sup id="cite_ref-Corbett_174_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corbett_174-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Members are arranged in a <a href="/wiki/Hemicycle_(chamber)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hemicycle (chamber)">hemicycle</a> according to their political groups (in the Common Assembly, prior to 1958, members sat alphabetically<sup id="cite_ref-Corbett_167_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corbett_167-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>) who are ordered mainly by left to right, but some smaller groups are placed towards the outer ring of the Parliament. All desks are equipped with microphones, headphones for translation and electronic voting equipment. The leaders of the groups sit on the front benches at the centre, and in the very centre is a podium for guest speakers. The remaining half of the circular chamber is primarily composed of the raised area where the President and staff sit. Further benches are provided between the sides of this area and the MEPs, these are taken up by the Council on the far left and the Commission on the far right. Both the Brussels and Strasbourg hemicycle roughly follow this layout with only minor differences.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The hemicycle design is a compromise between the different Parliamentary systems. The British-based system has the different groups directly facing each other while the French-based system is a semicircle (and the traditional German system had all members in rows facing a rostrum for speeches). Although the design is mainly based on a semicircle, the opposite ends of the spectrum do still face each other.<sup id="cite_ref-Corbett_167_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corbett_167-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> With access to the chamber limited, entrance is controlled by ushers who aid MEPs in the chamber (for example in delivering documents). The ushers can also occasionally act as a form of police in enforcing the President, for example in ejecting an MEP who is disrupting the session (although this is rare). The first head of protocol in the Parliament was French, so many of the duties in the Parliament are based on the French model first developed following the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. The 180 ushers are highly visible in the Parliament, dressed in black <a href="/wiki/Tailcoat" title="Tailcoat">tails</a> and wearing a silver chain, and are <a href="/wiki/EU_Concours" title="EU Concours">recruited</a> in the same manner as the <a href="/wiki/European_Civil_Service" title="European Civil Service">European civil service</a>. The President is allocated a personal usher.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="President_and_organisation">President and organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: President and organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg/170px-Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg/255px-Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg/340px-Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1775" data-file-height="2370" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Tajani_March_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tajani" title="Antonio Tajani">Antonio Tajani</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The President is essentially the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_(politics)" title="Speaker (politics)">speaker</a> of the Parliament and presides over the plenary when it is in session. The President\'s signature is required for all acts adopted by co-decision, including the EU budget. The President is also responsible for representing the Parliament externally, including in legal matters, and for the application of the rules of procedure. He or she is elected for two-and-a-half-year terms, meaning two elections per parliamentary term.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The President is currently <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tajani" title="Antonio Tajani">Antonio Tajani</a> MEP of the EPP.\n</p><p>In most countries, the protocol of the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> comes before all others; however, in the EU the Parliament is listed as the first institution, and hence the protocol of its president comes before any other European, or national, protocol. The gifts given to numerous visiting dignitaries depend upon the President. President <a href="/wiki/Josep_Borrell" title="Josep Borrell">Josep Borrell</a> MEP of Spain gave his counterparts a crystal cup created by an artist from Barcelona who had engraved upon it parts of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> among other things.<sup id="cite_ref-Protocol_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Protocol-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A number of notable figures have been President of the Parliament and its predecessors. The first President was <a href="/wiki/Paul-Henri_Spaak" title="Paul-Henri Spaak">Paul-Henri Spaak</a> MEP,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> one of the <a href="/wiki/Founding_fathers_of_the_European_Union" title="Founding fathers of the European Union">founding fathers of the Union</a>. Other founding fathers include <a href="/wiki/Alcide_de_Gasperi" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcide de Gasperi">Alcide de Gasperi</a> MEP and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a> MEP. The two female Presidents were <a href="/wiki/Simone_Veil" title="Simone Veil">Simone Veil</a> MEP in 1979 (first President of the elected Parliament) and <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Fontaine" title="Nicole Fontaine">Nicole Fontaine</a> MEP in 1999, both Frenchwomen.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The previous president, <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Buzek" title="Jerzy Buzek">Jerzy Buzek</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/East-Central_Europe" title="East-Central Europe">East-Central European</a> to lead an EU institution, a former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland" title="Prime Minister of Poland">Prime Minister of Poland</a> who rose out of the <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity</a> movement in Poland that helped overthrow communism in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the election of a President, the previous President (or, if unable to, one of the previous Vice-Presidents) presides over the chamber.<sup id="cite_ref-LeP_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeP-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Prior to 2009, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament#Oldest_member" title="President of the European Parliament">oldest member</a> fulfilled this role<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> but the rule was changed to prevent far-right French MEP <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Le_Pen" title="Jean-Marie Le Pen">Jean-Marie Le Pen</a> taking the chair.<sup id="cite_ref-LeP_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeP-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Below the President, there are 14 <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Vice President of the European Parliament">Vice-Presidents</a> who chair debates when the President is not in the chamber. There are a number of other bodies and posts responsible for the running of parliament besides these speakers. The two main bodies are the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_(European_Parliament)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bureau (European Parliament)">Bureau</a>, which is responsible for budgetary and administration issues, and the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_Presidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference of Presidents">Conference of Presidents</a> which is a governing body composed of the presidents of each of the parliament\'s political groups. Looking after the financial and administrative interests of members are five <a href="/wiki/Quaestor_(European_Parliament)" title="Quaestor (European Parliament)">Quaestors</a>.\n</p><p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the European Parliament budget was EUR 1.756 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> A 2008 report on the Parliament\'s finances highlighted certain overspending and miss-payments. Despite some MEPs calling for the report to be published, Parliamentary authorities had refused until an MEP broke confidentiality and leaked it.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Committees_and_delegations">Committees and delegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Committees and delegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Committees_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Committees of the European Parliament">Committees of the European Parliament</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CantinesEUbrussel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/CantinesEUbrussel.jpg/220px-CantinesEUbrussel.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/CantinesEUbrussel.jpg/330px-CantinesEUbrussel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/CantinesEUbrussel.jpg/440px-CantinesEUbrussel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3265" data-file-height="2409" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CantinesEUbrussel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>These "relocation boxes" of the European Parliament, called "cantines", are ready to be transported from <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> to <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> where a <a href="/wiki/Plenary_session" title="Plenary session">plenary session</a> will take place. Each month, the EP moves back and forth to meet the EU obligation to hold meetings also in France.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Parliament has 20 <a href="/wiki/Standing_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Standing Committee">Standing Committees</a> consisting of 25 to 73 MEPs each (reflecting the political make-up of the whole Parliament) including a chair, a bureau and secretariat. They meet twice a month in public to draw up, amend to adopt legislative proposals and reports to be presented to the plenary.<sup id="cite_ref-Organised_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Organised-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rapporteur" title="Rapporteur">rapporteurs</a> for a committee are supposed to present the view of the committee, although notably this has not always been the case. In the events leading to the resignation of the Santer Commission, the rapporteur went against the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Budgetary_Control" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee on Budgetary Control">Budgetary Control Committee\'s</a> narrow vote to discharge the budget, and urged the Parliament to reject it.<sup id="cite_ref-Ringe_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ringe-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Committees can also set up sub-committees (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Subcommittee_on_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Subcommittee on Human Rights">Subcommittee on Human Rights</a>) and temporary committees to deal with a specific topic (e.g. on <a href="/wiki/Extraordinary_rendition" title="Extraordinary rendition">extraordinary rendition</a>). The chairs of the Committees co-ordinate their work through the "<a href="/wiki/Committees_of_the_European_Parliament#Conference_of_Committee_Chairs" title="Committees of the European Parliament">Conference of Committee Chairmen</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Organised_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Organised-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> When co-decision was introduced it increased the Parliament\'s powers in a number of areas, but most notably those covered by the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_the_Environment,_Public_Health_and_Food_Safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Committee on the Environment, Public Health and Food Safety">Committee on the Environment, Public Health and Food Safety</a>. Previously this committee was considered by MEPs as a "<a href="/wiki/Cinderella" title="Cinderella">Cinderella</a> committee"; however, as it gained a new importance, it became more professional and rigorous, attracting increasing attention to its work.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoskyns_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoskyns-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/220px-Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/330px-Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg/440px-Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="972" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Committee_Room_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Brussels.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Committee room in the Parliament</div></div></div>\n<p>The nature of the committees differ from their national counterparts as, although smaller in comparison to those of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congressional_committee" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Congressional committee">United States Congress</a>, the European Parliament\'s committees are unusually large by European standards with between eight and twelve dedicated members of staff and three to four support staff. Considerable administration, archives and research resources are also at the disposal of the whole Parliament when needed.<sup id="cite_ref-Kreppel_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kreppel-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Delegations" class="mw-redirect" title="European Parliament Delegations">Delegations of the Parliament</a> are formed in a similar manner and are responsible for relations with Parliaments outside the EU. There are 34 delegations made up of around 15 MEPs, chairpersons of the delegations also cooperate in a conference like the committee chairs do. They include "Interparliamentary delegations" (maintain relations with Parliament outside the EU), "joint parliamentary committees" (maintaining relations with parliaments of states which are candidates or associates of the EU), the  delegation to the <a href="/wiki/ACP_EU_Joint_Parliamentary_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="ACP EU Joint Parliamentary Assembly">ACP EU Joint Parliamentary Assembly</a> and the delegation to the <a href="/wiki/Euro-Mediterranean_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="Euro-Mediterranean Parliamentary Assembly">Euro-Mediterranean Parliamentary Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Organised_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Organised-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> MEPs also participate in other international activities such as the <a href="/wiki/Euro-Latin_American_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="Euro-Latin American Parliamentary Assembly">Euro-Latin American Parliamentary Assembly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_Legislators%27_Dialogue" title="Transatlantic Legislators&#39; Dialogue">Transatlantic Legislators\' Dialogue</a> and through <a href="/wiki/Election_monitoring" title="Election monitoring">election observation</a> in third countries.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG/170px-2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG/255px-2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG/340px-2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_07_16_parlament_europejski_bruksela_47.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interpreting booths in the hemicycle simultaneously interpret debates between 24 languages</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intergroups">Intergroups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Intergroups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Intergroups_in_the_European_Parliament" title="Intergroups in the European Parliament">Intergroups in the European Parliament</a> are informal fora which gather MEPs from various political groups around any topic. They do not express the view of the European Parliament. They serve a double purpose: to address a topic which is transversal to several committees and in a less formal manner. Their daily secretariat can be run either through the office of MEPs or through interest groups, be them corporate lobbies or NGOs. The favored access to MEPs which the organization running the secretariat enjoys can be one explanation to the multiplication of Intergroups in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> They are now strictly regulated and financial support, direct or otherwise (via Secretariat staff, for example) must be officially specified in a declaration of financial interests.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Also Intergroups are established or renewed at the beginning of each legislature through a specific process. Indeed, the proposal for the constitution or renewal of an Intergroup must be supported by at least 3 political groups whose support is limited to a specific number of proposals in proportion to their size (for example, for the legislature 2014-2019, the EPP or S&amp;D political groups could support 22 proposals whereas the Greens/EFA or the EFDD political groups only 7).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Translation_and_interpretation">Translation and interpretation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Translation and interpretation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Speakers in the European Parliament are entitled to speak in any of the 24 official <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_European_Union" title="Languages of the European Union">languages of the European Union</a>, ranging from French and German to <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a> and Irish. Simultaneous interpreting is offered in all plenary sessions, and all final texts of legislation are translated. With twenty-four languages, the European Parliament is the most multilingual parliament in the world<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and the biggest employer of interpreters in the world (employing 350 full-time and 400 free-lancers when there is higher demand).<sup id="cite_ref-Interpreters_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interpreters-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Citizens may also address the Parliament in <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">Valencian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Usually a language is translated from a foreign tongue into a translator\'s native tongue. Due to the large number of languages, some being minor ones, since 1995 interpreting is sometimes done the opposite way, out of an interpreter\'s native tongue (the "retour" system). In addition, a speech in a minor language may be interpreted through a third language for lack of interpreters ("relay" interpreting)&#160;\xe2\x80\x94for example, when interpreting out of <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a> into <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Interpreters_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interpreters-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Due to the complexity of the issues, interpretation is not word for word. Instead, interpreters have to convey the political meaning of a speech, regardless of their own views. This requires detailed understanding of the politics and terms of the Parliament, involving a great deal of preparation beforehand (e.g. reading the documents in question). Difficulty can often arise when MEPs use profanities, jokes and word play or speak too fast.<sup id="cite_ref-Interpreters_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interpreters-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While some see speaking their native language as an important part of their identity, and can speak more fluently in debates, interpretation and its cost has been criticised by some. A 2006 report by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Stubb" title="Alexander Stubb">Alexander Stubb</a> MEP highlighted that by only using English, French and German costs could be reduced from <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>118,000 per day (for 21 languages then\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a> having not yet been included) to \xe2\x82\xac8,900 per day.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Some see the ideal single language as being English due to its widespread usage, although there has been a small-scale campaign to make French the reference language for all legal texts, due to the fact that it is more clear and precise for legal purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because the proceedings are translated into all of the official EU languages, they have been used to make a multilingual <a href="/wiki/Text_corpus" title="Text corpus">corpus</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Europarl_corpus" class="mw-redirect" title="Europarl corpus">Europarl</a>.  It is widely used to train <a href="/wiki/Statistical_machine_translation" title="Statistical machine translation">statistical machine translation</a> systems.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_costs">Annual costs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Annual costs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>According to the European Parliament website, the annual parliament budget for 2016 was \xe2\x82\xac1.838 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The main cost categories were:\n</p>\n<ul><li>34% - staff, interpretation and translation costs</li>\n<li>24% - information policy, IT, telecommunications</li>\n<li>23% - MEPs\' salaries, expenses, travel, offices and staff</li>\n<li>13% - buildings</li>\n<li>6% - political group activities</li></ul>\n<p>According to a European Parliament study prepared in 2013, the Strasbourg seat costs an extra \xe2\x82\xac103 million over maintaining a single location and according to the Court of Auditors an additional \xe2\x82\xac5 million is related to travel expenses caused by having two seats.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a comparison, the German lower house of parliament (<a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a>) is estimated to cost \xe2\x82\xac517 million in total for 2018, for a parliament with 709 members.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons" title="House of Commons">House of Commons</a> reported total annual costs in 2016-2017 of \xc2\xa3249 million (\xe2\x82\xac279 million). It had 650 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <i>The Economist</i>, the European Parliament costs more than the British, French and German parliaments combined. A quarter of the costs is estimated to be related to translation and interpretation costs (c. \xe2\x82\xac460 million) and the double seats are estimated to add an additional \xe2\x82\xac180 million a year.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> For a like-for-like comparison, these two cost blocks can be excluded. The resulting costs of c. \xe2\x82\xac1.2 billion a year are still more than double the German Bundestag\'s costs or more than four times the costs of the British House of Commons.\n</p><p>On 2 July 2018, MEPs rejected proposals to tighten the rules around the General Expenditure Allowance (GEA)<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seat">Seat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Seat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Location_of_European_Union_institutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Location of European Union institutions">Location of European Union institutions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Espace_L%C3%A9opold" title="Espace L\xc3\xa9opold">Espace L\xc3\xa9opold</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Parliament_in_Strasbourg" title="Seat of the European Parliament in Strasbourg">Seat of the European Parliament in Strasbourg</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style>\n<p>The Parliament is based in three different cities with numerous buildings. A protocol attached to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amsterdam" title="Treaty of Amsterdam">Treaty of Amsterdam</a> requires that 12 plenary sessions be held in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a> (none in August but two in September), which is the Parliament\'s official seat, while extra part sessions as well as committee meetings are held in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>. Luxembourg hosts the <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Secretariat of the European Parliament">Secretariat of the European Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaty_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaty-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The European Parliament is the only assembly in the world with more than one meeting place and one of the few that does not have the power to decide its own location.<sup id="cite_ref-Strange_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strange-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Strasbourg seat is seen as a symbol of reconciliation between France and Germany, the Strasbourg region having been fought over by the two countries in the past. However, the cost and inconvenience of having two seats is questioned. While Strasbourg is the official seat, and sits alongside the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union">Brussels is home to nearly all other major EU institutions</a>, with the majority of Parliament\'s work being carried out there. Critics have described the two-seat arrangement as a "travelling circus",<sup id="cite_ref-Seat_Green_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seat_Green-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and there is a strong movement to establish Brussels as the sole seat. This is because the other political institutions (the Commission, Council and European Council) are located there, and hence Brussels is treated as the \'<a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a>\' of the EU. This movement has received strong backing from numerous figures, including the Commission First-Vice President who stated that "something that was once a very positive symbol of the EU reuniting France and Germany has now become a negative symbol\xe2\x80\x94of wasting money, bureaucracy and the insanity of the Brussels institutions".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Party" title="European Green Party">Green Party</a> has also noted the environmental cost in a study led by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lambert" title="Jean Lambert">Jean Lambert</a> MEP and <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a> MEP; in addition to the extra 200&#160;million euro spent on the extra seat, there are over 20,268&#160;tonnes of additional carbon dioxide, undermining any environmental stance of the institution and the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Seat_Green_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seat_Green-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The campaign is further backed by a million-strong online petition started by <a href="/wiki/Cecilia_Malmstr%C3%B6m" title="Cecilia Malmstr\xc3\xb6m">Cecilia Malmstr\xc3\xb6m</a> MEP.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In August 2014, an assessment by the European Court of Auditors calculated that relocating the Strasbourg seat of the European Parliament to Brussels would save \xe2\x82\xac113.8 million per year.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, there were allegations of irregularities in the charges made by the city of Strasbourg on buildings the Parliament rented, thus further harming the case for the Strasbourg seat.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most MEPs prefer Brussels as a single base.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> A poll of MEPs found 89% of the respondents wanting a single seat, and 81% preferring Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Another, more academic, survey found 68% support.<sup id="cite_ref-Farrell_Powerful_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farrell_Powerful-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In July 2011, an absolute majority of MEPs voted in favour of a single seat.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In early 2011, the Parliament voted to scrap one of the Strasbourg sessions by holding two within a single week.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roland_Ries" title="Roland Ries">mayor of Strasbourg</a> officially reacted by stating "we will counter-attack by upturning the adversary\'s strength to our own profit, as a <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judoka</a> would do."<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> However, as Parliament\'s seat is now fixed by the treaties, it can only be changed by the Council acting unanimously, meaning that France could veto any move.<sup id="cite_ref-Strange_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strange-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The former <a href="/wiki/French_President" class="mw-redirect" title="French President">French President</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> has stated that the Strasbourg seat is "non-negotiable", and that France has no intention of surrendering the only EU Institution on French soil.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>  Given France\'s declared intention to veto any relocation to Brussels, some MEPs have advocated <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">civil disobedience</a> by refusing to take part in the monthly exodus to Strasbourg.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Channels_of_dialogue.2C_information.2C_and_communication_with_European_civil_society"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Channels_of_dialogue,_information,_and_communication_with_European_civil_society">Channels of dialogue, information, and communication with European civil society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Channels of dialogue, information, and communication with European civil society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Over the last few years, European institutions have committed to promoting transparency, openness, and the availability of information about their work.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In particular, transparency is regarded as pivotal to the action of European institutions and a general principle of EU law, to be applied to the activities of EU institutions in order to strengthen the Union\'s democratic foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The general principles of openness and transparency are reaffirmed in the articles 8 A, point 3 and 10.3 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> respectively, stating that "every citizen shall have the right to participate in the democratic life of the Union. Decisions shall be taken as openly and as closely as possible to the citizen".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, both treaties acknowledge the value of dialogue between citizens, representative associations, civil society, and European institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialogue_with_religious_and_non-confessional_organisations">Dialogue with religious and non-confessional organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dialogue with religious and non-confessional organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Article 17 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Functioning_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union">Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a> (TFEU) lays the juridical foundation for an open, transparent dialogue between European institutions and churches, religious associations, and non-confessional and philosophical organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In July 2014, in the beginning of the 8th term, then President of the European Parliament <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a> tasked <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Tajani" title="Antonio Tajani">Antonio Tajani</a>, then Vice-President, with implementing the dialogue with the religious and confessional organisations included in article 17.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In this framework, the European Parliament hosts high-level conferences on inter-religious dialogue, also with focus on current issues and in relation with parliamentary works.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament_Mediator_for_International_Parental_Child_Abduction">European Parliament Mediator for International Parental Child Abduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: European Parliament Mediator for International Parental Child Abduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The chair of European Parliament Mediator for International Parental Child Abduction was established in 1987 by initiative of British politician and MEP Charles <a href="/wiki/Henry_Plumb" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Plumb">Henry Plumb</a>, with the goal of helping minor children of international couples victim of parental abduction. The Mediator finds negotiated solutions in the higher interest of the minor when said minor is abducted by a parent following separation of the couple, regardless whether married or unmarried.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Since its institution, the chair has been held by <a href="/wiki/Mairead_McGuinness" title="Mairead McGuinness">Mairead McGuinness</a> (since 2014), Roberta Angelilli (2009-2014), Evelyne Gebhardt (2004-2009), Mary Banotti (1995-2004), and Marie-Claude Vayssade (1987-1994).<sup id="cite_ref-:1_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The Mediator\'s main task is to assist parents in finding a solution in the minor\'s best interest through mediation, i.e. a form of controversy resolution alternative to lawsuit. The Mediator is activated by request of a citizen and, after evaluating the request, starts a mediation process aimed at reaching an agreement. Once subscribed by both parties and the Mediator, the agreement is official. The nature of the agreement is that of a private contract between parties.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> In defining the agreement, the European Parliament offers the parties the juridical support necessary to reach a sound, lawful agreement based on legality and equity. The agreement can be ratified by the competent national courts and can also lay the foundation for consensual separation or divorce.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_151-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliamentary_Research_Service">European Parliamentary Research Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: European Parliamentary Research Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliamentary_Research_Service" title="European Parliamentary Research Service">European Parliamentary Research Service</a> (EPRS) is the European Parliament\'s in-house research department and think tank. It provides <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> \xe2\x80\x93 and, where appropriate, <a href="/wiki/Committees_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Committees of the European Parliament">parliamentary committees</a> \xe2\x80\x93 with independent, objective and authoritative analysis of, and research on, policy issues relating to the European Union, in order to assist them in their parliamentary work. It is also designed to increase Members\' and EP committees\' capacity to scrutinise and oversee the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Bodies_of_the_European_Union" title="Bodies of the European Union">EU executive bodies</a>.\n</p><p>EPRS aims to provide a comprehensive range of products and services, backed by specialist internal expertise and knowledge sources in all policy fields, so empowering Members and committees through knowledge and contributing to the Parliament\'s effectiveness and influence as an institution. In undertaking this work, the EPRS supports and promotes parliamentary outreach to the wider public, including dialogue with relevant stakeholders in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>\xe2\x80\x99s system of multi-level governance. All publications by EPRS are publicly available on the EP Think Tank platform.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Eurobarometer_of_the_European_Parliament">Eurobarometer of the European Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Eurobarometer of the European Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The European Parliament periodically commissions opinion polls and studies on public opinion trends in Member States to survey perceptions and expectations of citizens about its work and the overall activities of the European Union. Topics include citizens\' perception of the European Parliament\'s role, their knowledge of the institution, their sense of belonging in the European Union, opinions on European elections and European integration, identity, citizenship, political values, but also on current issues such as climate change, current economy and politics, etc.. <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> analyses seek to provide an overall picture of national situations, regional specificities, socio-demographic cleavages, and historical trends.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prizes">Prizes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Prizes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Annually, the European Parliament awards four prizes to individuals and organisations that distinguished themselves in the areas of human rights, film, youth projects, and European participation and citizenship.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sakharov_Prize_for_Freedom_of_Thought">Sakharov Prize for Freedom of Thought</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sakharov Prize for Freedom of Thought">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg/220px-Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg/330px-Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg/440px-Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4588" data-file-height="3059" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Remise_du_Prix_Sakharov_%C3%A0_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi_Strasbourg_22_octobre_2013-11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The ceremony of the <a href="/wiki/Sakharov_Prize" title="Sakharov Prize">Sakharov Prize</a> awarded to <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a>, in 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>With the <a href="/wiki/Sakharov_Prize_for_Freedom_of_Thought" class="mw-redirect" title="Sakharov Prize for Freedom of Thought">Sakharov Prize for Freedom of Thought</a>, created in 1998, the European Parliament supports human rights by awarding individuals that contribute to promoting human rights worldwide, thus raising awareness on human rights violations. Priorities include: protection of human rights and fundamental liberties, with particular focus on freedom of expression; protection of minority rights; compliance with international law; and development of democracy and authentic rule of law.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Charlemagne_Youth_Prize">European Charlemagne Youth Prize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: European Charlemagne Youth Prize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Charlemagne_Youth_Prize" title="European Charlemagne Youth Prize">European Charlemagne Youth Prize</a> seeks to encourage youth participation in the European integration process. It is awarded by the European Parliament and the Foundation of the International Charlemagne Prize of Aachen to youth projects aimed at nurturing common European identity and European citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="European_Citizens.27_Prize"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Citizens\'_Prize">European Citizens\' Prize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: European Citizens&#039; Prize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Citizens%27_Prize" title="European Citizens&#39; Prize">European Citizens\' Prize</a> is awarded by the European Parliament to activities and actions carried out by citizens and associations to promote integration between the citizens of EU member states and transnational cooperation projects in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_156-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LUX_Prize">LUX Prize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Parliament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: LUX Prize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 2007, the <a href="/wiki/LUX_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="LUX Prize">LUX Prize</a> is awarded by the European Parliament to films dealing with current topics of public European interest that encourage reflection on Europe and its future. Over time, the Lux Prize has become a prestigious cinema award which supports European film and production also outside the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Retrieved <span class="nowrap">29 April</span> 2016</span>. <q>A bicameral structure for the European Union has been proposed on numerous occasions. A frequent suggestion, and one designed to address the EU\xe2\x80\x99s alleged democratic deficit, is for a second chamber composed of national parliamentarians alongside the European Parliament. However, it is also argued that the EU already has a second chamber, the Council of the EU \xe2\x80\x93 representing Europe\xe2\x80\x99s nations, with the first chamber, the EP, representing its citizens.
